< review>
Nice little park tucked amongst the neighborhood. I can't comment much about the playground equipment since I didn't go over to it. However, they had a few basketball courts and solid picnic tables next to the grass. The field was large and had some lines painted on it for a small soccer field. The grass was a bit long but nice and green. We played "bubble soccer" and archery tag. Was a lot of fun and the park was perfect for it. Enough space and not a ton of people. I would go back with the family for a quick urban picnic. Lots of street parking for free. (If this review was helpful, please hit the like button below)</review>

< text>
I read good reviews of this place but upon visiting it just this one time my review won't be as glowing. It was a simple park, nothing fancy(which isn't a bad thing) a decent amount of roadside parking, nestled in a nice, quiet neighborhood. But ruining the peace and quiet for me on my walk with my girlfriend is the noise coming from the basketball court end of the park. A bunch of dudes cranking a radio with loud profanities coming out of their mouth at the rate of every other word. Unfortunately they can't respect the neighborhood they're in. Makes it an ugly side of the park, but luckily avoided by simply not going down that end. I wonder what the residents of the nearby area think when they hear that going on.
I'll go back again though because it's close by and without the noisy people it's a pretty nice walk.< /text>

< Text>
Loved my experience here at Mako. I wanted to make a sushi stop while I was in Little Tokyo and happened to pass this as I was heading to the Blue Whale (jazz venue) and decided to walk in. What a treat it was! The staff and customers were so happy and it felt very relaxing and altogether pleasant.

The sushi was pricey, but overall very good and high quality cuts made in front of you. The real winner was the tofu miso soup and sake they had. Overall, I would recommend this restaurant to anyone who is looking for a nice experience in a sushi spot.</Text>

<gmap_id>0x80c2c6488ea39f65:0xa630981db69cf93</gmap_id><pictures>None<//pictures><Text>Mako is truly a classic Japanese restaurant...It's plucked out of a traditional Japanese neighborhood somewhere in To-kyo- no Shita Machi or old town Tokyo, on an out of the way "Roji"/small pathway & magically placed here in downtown LA.

At the entry way there is the time honoured Noren (noh ren)/short curtain that indicates that the store is open for business.  The Noren seems to function as a portal or divide between the sacredness of what lies within & the profanity of the outside world.

Walk through the Noren & enter the foyer, & you will hear the cheerful greeting of "Irasshaimase" Welcome.   Kimono clad ladies w/ smiles on their faces will lead you to either the tables or the Sushi bar of your choosing.

I always call ahead to reserve a spot since it allows me to know if there will be a wait or not.  Also, even if the restaurant is not full, I still like to give the restaurant the notice that I am coming as a courtesy.

I like sitting at the Sushi bar since you can see how the Namamono (raw foods) are prepared, & you can talk to Mako,the owner, for suggestions about the food as well as what specialty premium Sake will pair w/ the foods that were ordered.  I'm always impressed by the high quality of their "Neta" (the seafood) used on their sushi, & their cooked foods show a sophisticated hand.

Their mini Ishi Yaki stone grill sizzlingly hot w/ either beef or scallops adds an air of excitement especially with a person you want to impress.  Same (sah meh) no Nankotsu/shark cartilage in a Japanese salty, agrodolce plum sauce is most unusual to accompany Sake (sah keh) or Japanese beer as an appetizer.

Mako has all the various grades & parts of the Hon Maguro/blue fin tuna which is probably the most esteemed fish in all of the Sushi/Sashimi universe.  Mouth feel is a meaty yet velvety smoothness almost bordering on the taste of beef carpaccio or tartar.  A touch of Wasabi acts as a palate cleanser, & Sho-yu (soy sauce) adds more Umami, that 5th flavour component that is ineffable yet adds richness & meatiness.

Chu-Toro & O-Toro are fattier sections of the Hon Maguro.  O-Toro is comparable to delicately fat inscribed premium prime beef.  Chu-Toro being a bit less fatty w/ more of a meat component.

Nihon no Tai, Japanese Red Snapper, is another example of the pristine, flavourful nature of the absolutely fresh fish. The white, translucent soft, velvety flesh of the Tai is given a textural contrast by the inclusion of the skin including the scales which are slightly seared.

Mako's Sushi rice is another subtle demonstration on his nuanced mastery of the Sushi universe.  The rice grains come out individually intact & the mouthfeel is slightly al dente w/ a texture that gives way to a firm softness ideal as a contrast to the usually softer textures.

Rice is a touch "nutty" & addition of a soupcon of Japanese vinegar highlights in the rice a slight pleasant sweetness.  Rice is compressed w/ just the right pressure so that the Nigiri maintains its integrity but falls apart in the mouth.  Truly exemplary Sushi rice by a Meister Chef.

You have to try out Mako yourself to see if what I am relating is fiction or fact.  I have been to such temples of Sushi such as Asanebo in the Valley, Sushi Sasabune, Sushi Zo in West Los Angeles, Bar Nozawa at Sugarfish in Beverly Hills as well as Sushi Go, Hama Sushi, Komasa, over rated Sushi Gen in Little Tokyo.

But for me, Mako stands out in terms of quality & bang for the bucks.  Don't get me wrong, Mako is not cheap, but I come out w/ a bit more change at Mako than at the other mentioned places.

Mako, Mayumi, & the rest of the crew  really make you feel welcome...but just remember that good food takes time to prepare so plan on staying a while to enjoy the food and the old school ambience that Mako and Little Tokyo have to offer.  Like most of the good things in life, the experience at Mako Sushi shouldn't be rushed but savoured.< /Text><user_name>Gary I.<//user_name><resp>None<//resp><Date>1535163731519</Date>< rate>
5< /rate>

< Review>
Food was deliciously flavorful, portion sizes were large for the prices paid, interior is cute and clean, staff were nice, bathrooms were well kept. Parking lot is small and shared with other businesses so I'd imagine it could get busy during peak times

Came here for a late lunch over the weekend, the place wasn't too busy and we were seated immediately. Our orders came quickly. The noodles here are A++, the perfect consistency and chewiness. The coconut rice was delicious as well! Definitely will be back to try the rest of the menu items!</Review>

< rate>

< Text>
Wow. I lived in Indonesia with my family for 4 years and I’ve been disappointed by every Indonesian place I’ve eaten outside of Indonesia. Not any more. I’ve driven past Uncle Fung many times and  ever had the opportunity to go in, but today was the day. I went with my family and everyone was impressed. We tried: sate, gado-gado, Ayam goreng kalasan, both the curry and coconut rice, the laksa mie, and one of the other mie options. This was easily the best Indonesian (and Singaporean) food I’ve eaten outside of Indonesia, and it was actually better than a lot of the Indonesian food I’ve eaten IN Indonesia. The peanut sauce was on point, the laksa was the best I’ve ever had, the sambal was right (this is important!). They just nailed it. I’ll be back for sure.

Even though it pains me to pay US prices for Indonesian food, the food was reasonably priced for the location. Service was quick, efficient and friendly. I can’t wait to go back!< /Text>

<name>Rodney S< /name>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
<resp>None</resp><Gmap_id>0x80dd2be74ce6de2f:0x6bdeaf981a297ac6</Gmap_id>< time>
1550444815124<//time>
< review>
Laksa love here!  Whole Laksa love!

Man, do I love me some laksa mee.   I remember serving jury duty at the Alhambra courthouse, and two of my lunch breaks were spent at Borneo Kalimantan Cuisine, where I had the most wonderful fortune of having laksa mee Singapore  for the very first time.  Perturbed in finding an eatery closer to me, I now have an option not far at all from my residence.

Buena Park is home to the second Uncle Fung Borneo Eatery, with the first being in Long Beach.  On a cold, rainy day, laksa mee Singapore beckoned me into it's warm, loving arms & I just had to satisfy my craving.

Laksa mee Singapore (w/ homemade egg noodles)-
Choice of either beehoon (thin rice noodles), kway teow (flat rice noodles) or mee (homemade egg noodles).  Hey, when something's homemade, you gotta get dat, yo.  The creamy, savory, coconut milk curry broth is accentuated with shrimp, fish cake, fried tofu, hardboiled egg, sweet corn, scallions & fried shallot.  Love at first slurp!  Think ramen, but kicked up a notch with rich coconut milk.  The spices, the right amount of heat to appease spicy lovers, yet not enough to deter the non-spice lovers, the perfectly al dente noodles.  Like a seasoned ensemble cast, it all just works.  Probably my favorite soup dish, period!

Service was good.  I was quickly attended to when ordering and after the short wait for my piping hot bowl of soup to come out.  A fair amount of seating, Uncle Fung is best suited for smaller sized parties.

Parking is via a small private lot.  There is an adjacent parking lot, but I believe it's only for the bank & IHOP, with signs declaring so.  Street parking is also available behind the restaurant.  Uncle Fung is located right across La Palma Ave. from the Buena Park Downtown Mall.

Laksa for lunch?  Why not?  Uncle Fung Borneo Eatery hits the spot when I need to satisfy my laksa mee craving.  At a little over $10 a bowl, and being minutes away, Uncle Fung has become one of my go-to spots for good grub.  Perhaps, I may explore the rest of the menu, say the roti or chicken satay, but I don't foresee ever dining at Uncle Fung without having a bowl of laksa mee Singapore front & center on my table.

Highly recommend!
NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM<//review>

< date>
1578418843881<//date>
<Rating>5< /Rating><Review>If you want to get a free tour of Stanford University, then here you are. The Campus Walking Tour departs from the Stanford Visitor Center. It is a great introduction for first-time visitors and tourists. Excursions spend 7 days a week  2 times a day 11:30 a.m. & 3:30 p.m. No reservations are required for parties of 8 or fewer.
This tour covers central campus, including:
The Main Quad (historic and academic center of campus, including the school of Humanities & Sciences)
Memorial Church
Engineering Quad
White Plaza (student activities area, including the Bookstore, Student Store, Old Union, and Tresidder Memorial Union)
I advise everyone to visit a free tour.

In this center you can also leave things and take a map of the territory of the university. The staff is polite, kind and friendly.

The center is accessible for wheelchairs.

#letsguide #familyfriendly #kidsfriendly #accessibility< /Review>< pics>

< Review>
You can show up to any of the walking tours without a reservation. They have signs posted on campus. The engineering tour meets at the steps of the Packard building.
The Arts and Humanity tour meets at the clock tower.

The tour leaders are very knowledgeable, however they tend to get distracted by the attendees while walking. If you want to learn about the campus, make sure to ask lots of questions.< /Review>

<username>B Roy Chaudhary< /username><date>1539218353548<//date><rate>5< /rate>< text>
Stanford visitor Centre run a very efficient system for managing visitor tours. The website has a lot of details to plan things before hand. Once in the visitor centre they have present Stanford student, who give up their time on a voluntary basis, take the visitors in groups walking around the campus and detail the history and significance of all things Stanford. Highly recommended for any aspiring students.  Enjoy.

Please consider tapping the like button below if this review was helpful. Thanks.</text>

(Translated by Google) Stanford University was founded in 1891 by the then California senator and governor of railroad tycoon Leeland Stanford and his wife Jane Stanford. This is in memory of their son who died on the eve of his 16th birthday due to typhoid fever (Leland Stanford, Jr.). Stanford University is a school for the freedom of men, women and religion, and all tuition fees were waived until the 1930s. [13] However, charges began only after the death of Leland Stanford in 1893 and the San Francisco earthquake that caused major damage to the campus in 1906, which caused severe financial difficulties for the school. [14] After the Second World War, Frederick Terman, then the school dean, fully supported the entrepreneurial spirit of alumni and faculty, hoping to build a self-sufficient local industry, which is also the origin of Silicon Valley today.

The school's campus is located northwest of Silicon Valley, near Palo Alto. [15] Since the 1970s, Stanford has become the home of the SLAC National Accelerator Laboratory in the United States, and the origin of one of the Advanced Research Projects Agency networks (the prototype of the Internet). [16] The school's various academic departments are grouped into seven academic colleges, while other assets, including bioconservation areas and accelerated laboratories, are located outside the main campus. [6] This school is also one of the richest educational institutions and is the first university to receive a donation increase of more than one billion US dollars in one year. [17]

Stanford is a university with a high accommodation rate and high selectivity, with graduate courses more diverse than undergraduates. Stanford students participate in different sports competitions through 36 teams, which is one of the two private universities of the Pacific Twelve Schools Alliance. As of 2018, Stanford students and alumni have won 270 Olympic medals, including 139 gold medals, at previous Olympics. [18] The school team has won 104 university sports association championships, ranking second in many universities. Since 1994-95, he has also been the annual winner of the National College Sports Directors Cup. [19]

As of October 2019, Stanford University alumni, professors and researchers have produced a total of 83 Nobel Prize winners, 8 Fields Prize winners and 27 Turing Prize winners. [Note 2] Stanford has cultivated many famous people. Its alumni include 30 wealthy entrepreneurs and 17 astronauts. It is also one of the institutions that trains the most members of the United States Congress. [20] [21] Stanford alumni have founded many famous companies around the world, such as: Google, Yahoo, HP, Cisco Systems, Nike, Sun Microsystems, TSMC, Nvidia, EA, etc. Total equivalent to the tenth largest economic system in the world (as of 2011)

(Original)
史丹佛大學於1891年由時任加州參議員及州長的鐵路大亨利蘭·史丹佛和他的妻子簡·萊思羅普·史丹佛（英語：Jane Stanford）創辦。這是為了紀念他們因傷寒而於16歲生日前夕去世的兒子（小利蘭·史丹佛（英語：Leland Stanford, Jr.））。史丹佛大學為男女及宗教自由的學校，在1930年代前所有學費全免。[13]可是，1893年利蘭·史丹佛的逝世及1906年對校園造成重大損毀的舊金山大地震，為該校帶來嚴重的財政困難後才開始收費。[14]二次世界大戰後，時任學校教務長的弗雷德里克·特曼全力支持校友與教職員的企業精神，希望能建立一個自給自足的本地工業，這也是現今矽谷的源流。

學校的校園位於矽谷的西北方，鄰近帕羅奧圖。[15]自上世紀七十年代，史丹佛成為了美國SLAC國家加速器實驗室的所在地，及其中一個高等研究計劃署網路（網際網路雛形）的起源地。[16]校方的各個學術部門被歸入七所學術學院內，而包括生物保育區及加速實驗室在內的其他資產則設於主校區之外。[6] 此校同時為最富有的教育機構之一，並為第一所在一年內獲得超過十億美元捐款升幅的大學。[17]

史丹佛為一所擁有高住宿率及高選擇性的大學，當中的研究生課程較本科的多元化。史丹佛學生透過36支代表隊參與不同的體育競賽，其為兩所太平洋十二校聯盟的私立大學之一。截止2018年，史丹佛大學的學生和校友在歷屆奧運會上贏得了包括139枚金牌在內的270枚奧運獎牌。[18]有關校隊曾奪得過104次大學體育協會賽事的冠軍，成績於眾多大學中位列第二。自1994-95年起，其亦一直為全國大學體育競技董事杯的年度得主。[19]

截止2019年10月，史丹佛大學的校友、教授及研究人員中，共產生了83名諾貝爾獎得主、8位菲爾茲獎得主以及27位圖靈獎得主。[註 2]史丹佛培養了不少著名人士，其校友涵蓋30名富豪企業家及17名太空員，亦為培養最多美國國會成員的院校之一。[20][21]史丹佛校友在世界各地創辦了眾多著名的公司機構，如：谷歌、雅虎、惠普、思科系統、耐克、昇陽電腦、台積電、英偉達、藝電等等，這些企業的資金合計相等於全球第十大經濟體系（截止2011年）<//review>
